  └───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

  STEP 6 — PBO  (Probability of Backtest Overfitting)
  CSCV  ·  Bailey, Borwein, Lopez de Prado & Zhu (2015)
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
  PBO — PROBABILITY OF BACKTEST OVERFITTING  [All filter modes]
  CSCV method · Bailey et al. (2015) · J. Computational Finance
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
  Strategies (N)        : 4
  Trading days (T)      : 398  (sub-period len=24d, S=16)
  Combinations C(S,S/2) : 12,870

  PBO                   : 0.270  (27.0%)
  Grade                 : ⚠  LOW RESOLUTION (N=4 < 10 — see warnings)
  Performance Degradation (PD) : +0.3519  Sharpe drop train→test
  Probability of Loss (POL)    : 0.000  (0.0%)  (test Sharpe of winner < 0)
  Discrete logit values (4) : -1.9459  -0.5108  +0.5108  +1.9459

  ── Training-window win counts ──
  A - Tail Guardrail                        10169×  ( 79.0%)  ███████████████████████████████████████
  A - Calendar Filter                        2005×  ( 15.6%)  ███████
  A - No Filter                               696×  (  5.4%)  ██
  A - Volatility                                0×  (  0.0%)  

  ── Logit(ω) distribution (λ_c = log(rank/(N−rank))) ──
  Mean  : +0.7812    Median: +1.9459
  Stdev : 1.5491     Range : [-1.9459, +1.9459]
  λ < 0 : 3478 / 12870  = PBO
  λ = 0 :    0 / 12870  (winner ranked at exact median)
  λ > 0 : 9392 / 12870

  ── Warnings ──
  ⚠  LOW RESOLUTION: N=4 strategies means logit(ω) can only take 4
       discrete values (-1.9459, -0.5108, +0.5108, +1.9459). PBO=0.270
       reflects which of these 4 buckets the training winner falls into
       — not a continuous probability. Grade bands are not reliable at
       N < 10.

  ⚠  STRUCTURAL BIAS: when the N strategies are filter variants of
       the same base strategy, unfiltered variants have more active
       trading days per sub-period, which mechanically inflates their
       sub-period Sharpe. This causes unfiltered variants to win more
       training splits even when filtered variants are stronger over
       the full period. Interpret win counts with this in mind.

  ── Interpretation ──
  With N=4 strategies the logit(ω) distribution has only 4
  discrete values, so PBO grade bands (Low / Moderate / High) are
  not statistically meaningful here.
  
  What this result DOES tell you:
    · In 27% of train/test splits the filter with the best
      in-sample Sharpe did NOT rank in the top half out-of-sample.
      → Filter selection by in-sample Sharpe alone is unstable.
    · The unfiltered variant dominates training splits because it
      has more active trading days per sub-period, mechanically
      inflating its sub-period Sharpe (active-day structural bias).
    · This is expected behaviour, not evidence of overfitting.
  
  What this result does NOT tell you:
    · It does NOT mean the underlying strategy is overfit.
    · POL = 0% means the training winner ALWAYS had positive
      test Sharpe — the strategy was profitable in every OOS window.
  
  Recommended action:
    · To get a meaningful PBO, run CSCV across a large grid of
      independently-tuned parameter configurations (N ≥ 20 ideally),
      not across filter variants of the same base strategy.
    · Use POL and PD as the primary overfitting diagnostics here.
